width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -1.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 3.003em;"></span></span></nobr></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-4">{\rm{DataRate}}=\left(n\times x\times{1\over f_{{\rm MCU-CLK}}}\right)^{-1}\eqno{\hbox{(1)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">{\rm{DataRate}}=\left(n\times x\times{1\over f_{{\rm MCU-CLK}}}\right)^{-1}\eqno{\hbox{(1)}}</span></span></disp-formula>
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig4"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808172/4808172-fig-4-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808172/4808172-fig-4-small.gif" alt="Figure 4" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 4. </b><fig><p>COMM module inputs and output (time axis not per scale).</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4808172/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div> where <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-5-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-87" role="math" style="width: 0.664em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.604em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.54em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-88"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-89" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">x</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.67em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-5">x</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the cycles-per-clock delay in implementing one instruction by the program counter, which was set to the lowest allowable value of 4, as permitted by the MCU architecture in order to give the fastest data rate. The parameter <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-6-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-90" role="math" style="width: 4.808em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.327em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1004.33em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-91"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-92"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.327em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.387em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-93" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">f<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.841em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-94"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-95"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-96"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-97"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-98" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">M</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-99" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">C</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-100" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">U</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-101" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">â</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-102" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">C</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-103" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">L</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-104" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">K</span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-6">f_{{\rm MCU-CLK}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> in <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn1" href="#deqn1" class="fulltext-link">(1)</a> is the clock frequency of the MCU. To minimize the number of the external components, it was decided to use the integrated Colpitts oscillator internal to the MCU, which had a maximum clock frequency of 4 MHz for both monopole- and dipole-based designs. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 4</a> shows the MCU generated signals at the COMM enable and PA enable inputs of the COMM module. The sinusoidal waveform in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 4</a> is the final ASK modulated RF output of the PA, which is also the sensor data that is fed into the antenna.<p></p><p>Two sub-carrier cycle Miller bit encoded signals are transmitted at data rates in excess of 5 kb/s from tags to reader as per RFID UHF Gen-2 protocols <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_2b">[8]</a>. Based on <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn1" href="#deqn1" class="fulltext-link">(1)</a>, any value of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-7-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-105" role="math" style="width: 0.664em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.604em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.6em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-106"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-107" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">n</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.67em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-7">n</script></tex-math></inline-formula> less than 200 should yield a data rate of greater than 5 kb/s for an MCU clock frequency of 4 MHz. For the module prototypes presented in this paper, the value of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-8-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-108" role="math" style="width: 0.664em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.604em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.6em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-109"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-110" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">n</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.67em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-8">n</script></tex-math></inline-formula> that was coded in the MCU firmware was 146, which yielded a data rate of 6.8 kb/s, as was verified by the wireless link measurement shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 5</a>. The data rate is the reciprocal of the measured bit duration shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 5</a>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig5"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808172/4808172-fig-5-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808172/4808172-fig-5-small.gif" alt="Figure 5" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 5. </b><fig><p>RTSA measured ASK modulated signal with 50% duty cycle (power versus time).</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4808172/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig6"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808172/4808172-fig-6-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808172/4808172-fig-6-small.gif" alt="Figure 6" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 6. </b><fig><p>Prototying board for loadâpull analysis and in-circuit programming <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_2b">[12]</a>.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4808172/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>To verify the correct operation of the MCU firmware and its interoperability with the COMM module, a prototype of the entire system was implemented on a copper-clad Duroid board, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 6</a>. Interfaces were also provided to the IC on the prototype board to enable in-circuit programming and debugging of the MCU. The PA output was connected to a printed circuit board (PCB)-mounted subminiature A (SMA) connector through a coplanar waveguide with a grond plane (CPW-G) feed for the RF baud rate and PA characterization measurements described in the following section.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec2c"><h3>C. Amplifier (PA) Characterization</h3><p>The range of the wireless transfer is directly proportional to the amount of power transferred from the amplifier in the transmitter front end to the antenna. Any impedance mismatch between the two can lead to the reflection of a part of the power intended to radiate out of the antenna, thereby minimizing the range. Instead of designing the antenna to a 50-<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-9-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-111" role="math" style="width: 0.844em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.66em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-112"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-113" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Î©</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-9">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> match, it was decided to design it to the optimum impedance looking out of the amplifier (PA) in the transmitter. Doing so would eliminate the need for a matching network, minimizing series losses, as well as the number of components used in the design, thus leading to a more compact design.</p><p>To determine the optimum load impedance looking out of the PA in the transmitter, a loadâpull analysis was performed on it at three different frequencies of 860, 904.4, and 925 MHz <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_2c">[11]</a>, all of which fall within the unlicensed UHF frequency bands in the U.S. and Europe used for RFID communication <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_2c">[5]</a>. The analysis was carried out for a fixed-bias point for which the PA output was biased at the power supply voltage of 3 V with an RF choke in between to maximize drain collector efficiency for class A operation suitable for ASK modulation <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_2c">[11]</a>. The setup used for this measurement is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 7</a>. For this measurement, the test module, built on Duroid and shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 6</a>, was used.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig7"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808172/4808172-fig-7-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808172/4808172-fig-7-small.gif" alt="Figure 7" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 7. </b><fig><p>Measurement setup for loadâpull characterization of integrated PA.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4808172/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full table" id="table1"><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">TableÂ I </b>LoadâPull Results<div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808172/4808172-table-1-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808172/4808172-table-1-small.gif" alt="Table " /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div></div>
<p></p><p>For the loadâpull measurements, the microcontroller was programmed to operate in the UNMOD mode during which it would continuously enable the RF PA, which would send a constant unmodulated sinusoidal signal at the transmitter output. The loadâpull tuner was tuned to different impedances to locate its impedance value <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-10-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-114" role="math" style="width: 3.547em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.186em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1003.07em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-115"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-116" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-117"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.405em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-118"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-119"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-120" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-121"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-122"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-123" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-124" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">u</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-125" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">n</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-126" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">e</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-127" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">r</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-128" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-10">({Z}_{\rm tuner})</script></tex-math></inline-formula> at which the PA gave out maximum power <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_2c">[11]</a>, which was read off the series power meter (see <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 6</a>). The loss in the measurement setup, i.e., the RF tuner, the â20-dB coupler, and the cables, were measured separately at each one of the three measurement frequencies and added to the power output measured with the power meter to get the optimum output power shown in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table1" class="fulltext-link">TableÂ I</a>. An Agilent E4438C vector signal generator (VSG) was used to generate the input RF signal, while the output power was measured using the Agilent E4419B rpm power meter. A portion of the output power was coupled to an Agilent E4404B spectrum analyzer to ensure that the power meter was measuring the output power at the correct output RF frequency. The loadâpull tuner used was a Maury model 1643-N.</p><p>The effects of the SMA connector, coplanar waveguide (CPW) feed, the series capacitor, and bias circuitry were deembedded at various points along the output of the circuit to determine the optimum impedance referenced at the IC output <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-11-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-129" role="math" style="width: 3.967em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.547em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1003.43em 2.706em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-130"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-131" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-132"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.766em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-133"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-134"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-135" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-136"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-137"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-138"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-139"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-140" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">L</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-141" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">â</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-142" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">o</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-143" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">p</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-144" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-145" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.397em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-11">({Z}_{{\rm L-opt}})</script></tex-math></inline-formula> after accounting for the impedance of the bias circuit. The impedance of the bias circuit <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-12-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-146" role="math" style="width: 3.066em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.766em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1002.65em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-147"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-148" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-149"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.985em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-150"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-151"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-152" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-153"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-154"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-155" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">b</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-156" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">i</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-157" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">a</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-158" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">s</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-159" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-12">({Z}_{\rm bias})</script></tex-math></inline-formula> was determined by measuring the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-13-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-160" role="math" style="width: 0.724em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.664em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.66em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-161"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-162" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">S<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-13">S</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-parameters of the RF choke and bias coupling capacitors from which their respective impedances were determined at 860, 904.4, and 925 MHz that were then modeled in the bias circuitry using Agilent's Advanced Design System (ADS) software. The equivalent circuit looking out of the PA on the prototyping board that had to be deembedded for the loadâpull test setup is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 8</a>. The results of the loadâpull analysis are shown in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table1" class="fulltext-link">TableÂ I</a>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig8"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808172/4808172-fig-8-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808172/4808172-fig-8-small.gif" alt="Figure 8" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 8. </b><fig><p>Equivalent circuit looking out of the RF PA.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4808172/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec3"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION III.</div><h2>Antenna Design and Circuit Integration</h2></div><p>The output impedances of the PA determined during the loadâpull characterization were then used to design power-optimized dipole and monopole antennas for the wireless transmitters. The antennas were designed to resonate close to 904.4 MHz with the hopes of achieving a return loss bandwidth that would cover the extreme frequencies of 860 and 925 MHz as well. The antennas were inkjet printed on the paper substrates along with the circuit itself.</p><div class="section_2" id="sec3a"><h3>A. Single-Layer Dipole Antenna</h3><p>Half-wavelength dipole antennas are among the most commonly used antennas for RFID applications. They can be folded and tapered for more compact size and wider bandwidth <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref13" id="context_ref_13_3a">[13]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref14" id="context_ref_14_3a">[14]</a>. In addition, half-wavelength dipole antennas have a radiation resistance of 75 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-14-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-163" role="math" style="width: 0.844em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.66em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-164"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-165" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Î©</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-14">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref15" id="context_ref_15_3a">[15]</a>, which is close to the real part of the optimum load impedance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-15-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-166" role="math" style="width: 3.967em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.547em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1003.43em 2.706em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-167"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-168" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-169"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.766em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-170"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-171"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-172" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-173"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-174"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-175"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-176"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-177" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">L</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-178" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">â</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-179" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">o</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-180" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">p</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-181" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-182" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.397em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-15">({Z}_{{\rm L-opt}})</script></tex-math></inline-formula> looking out of the PA at 904.4 MHz listed in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table1" class="fulltext-link">TableÂ I</a> making for an easier impedance match. For the first wireless sensor module prototype, a tapering U-shaped half wavelength dipole structure described in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_3a">[12]</a> and <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref16" id="context_ref_16_3a">[16]</a> was chosen for the antenna. The circuit layout was to be placed in the space within the U-shape of the antenna to make the size of the complete module more compact <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_3a">[3]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref16" id="context_ref_16_3a">[16]</a>.</p><p>The antenna was to be printed on a single layer of a paper substrate along with the circuit layout using an inket-printing technique <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_3a">[6]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref16" id="context_ref_16_3a">[16]</a>â<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref17" id="context_ref_17_3a">[17]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref18" id="context_ref_18_3a">[18]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref19" id="context_ref_19_3a">[19]</a>. The biggest challenge on using a dipole antenna this way was integrating and sufficiently isolating it from the circuit of the sensor module within its U-shape, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 9</a>. The close vicinity of the antenna with respect to the circuit would alter its mutual impedance, which could cause an impedance mismatch with the PA, thereby reducing the amount of power radiated along with the transmitted range <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref15" id="context_ref_15_3a">[15]</a>. To ensure an impedance match, the antenna was optimized so that the impedance looking out of the PA would be close to its optimum value <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-16-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-183" role="math" style="width: 3.967em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.547em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1003.43em 2.706em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-184"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-185" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-186"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.766em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-187"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-188"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-189" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-190"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-191"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-192"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-193"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-194" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">L</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-195" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">â</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-196" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">o</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-197" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">p</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-198" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-199" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.397em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-16">({Z}_{{\rm L-opt}})</script></tex-math></inline-formula> at 904.4 MHz (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-17-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-200" role="math" style="width: 7.511em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 6.73em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1006.67em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-201"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-202" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">60.1</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-203" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">â</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-204" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic; padding-left: 0.243em;">j</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-205" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">73.51</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-206" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Â </span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-207" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Î©</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-17">60.1-j73.51\ \Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) with the sensor module circuitry connected within the space between the antenna arms.</p><p>
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig9"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808172/4808172-fig-9-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808172/4808172-fig-9-small.gif" alt="Figure 9" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 9. </b><fig><p>Dipole-based module topology.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4808172/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig10"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808172/4808172-fig-10-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808172/4808172-fig-10-small.gif" alt="Figure 10" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 10. </b><fig><p>Simulated return loss of the dipole antenna connected to the circuit.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4808172/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div> In addition, RF chokes (L1, L2) were used at several points in the circuit to minimize RF signals, meant to travel between the antenna and PA, from creeping into the positive power supply trace of the battery that was used to bias the PA (antenna terminals) and power up the MCU. RF chokes could not, however, be placed between the negative terminal of the antenna (also the PA ground) and the negative power supply of the battery because doing so would reduce the gain of the single-ended PA and alter the optimum load impedance determined in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table1" class="fulltext-link">TableÂ I</a> <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_3a">[11]</a>. An RF choke (L3) was placed between the RF crystal and the negative power supply of the battery to isolate it from RF signals from the antenna.<p></p><p>The entire structure of the module including the antenna and the circuit layout was built using Ansoft's HFSS 3-D EM solver, which was also used to optimize the antenna. Lumped resistor/inductor/capacitor (RLC) boundaries with values equal to the measured values of inductors L1, L2,and L3 at 904.4 MHz were used to simulate the RF chokes in the circuit, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 9</a>. A lumped port was used as the RF power source in place of the PA to excite the antenna. The final dipole antenna design along with the circuit in between had a dimension of 9.5 Ã 5 sq. cm.</p><p>The simulated return loss or <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-18-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-208" role="math" style="width: 1.565em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.38em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-209"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-210"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-211"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-212"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-213" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">S<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-214"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-215"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-216" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">11</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-18">{S}_{11}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> for the antenna with respect to the PA's optimum load impedance (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-19-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-217" role="math" style="width: 7.15em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 6.429em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1006.37em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-218"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-219" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">60.1</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-220" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">â</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-221" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic; padding-left: 0.243em;">j</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-222" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">73.51</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-223" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Î©</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-19">60.1-j73.51 \Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig10" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 10</a>, and shows a good impedance match at the design frequency of 904.4 MHz with a â10-dB bandwidth of 60 MHz. The simulated and measured radiation pattern are shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig11" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 11</a> and show reasonably good agreement. A maximum simulated directivity of 1.54 dB was achieved.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec3b"><h3>B. Double-Layer Monopole Antenna</h3><p>
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig11"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808172/4808172-fig-11-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808172/4808172-fig-11-small.gif" alt="Figure 11" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 11. </b><fig><p>Normalized 2-D far-field radiation plots of simulation and chamber measurement of the dipole-based printed sensor module.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4808172/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div> Many of the drawbacks with the dipole-based module can be eliminated by using a monopole-based structure. The monopole uses its ground planes as a radiating surface, which can also be used to shield any circuitry behind it. The monopole antenna also does not require a differentially fed input signal like the dipole, which was ideal for the PA since its output was single ended.<p></p><p>The circuit for the monopole was laid out on two layers, which helped minimize the size of the circuit topology by avoiding the long power supply traces that had to be used on the single-layer dipole-based module. The top layer contained the printed antenna and most of the circuit components for the module. The bottom layer contained an Li-ion cell and the power supply traces, which were routed to the top layer through drilled vias.</p><p>The monopole antenna had a planar CPW-G fed wideband structure with a rectangular radiator to achieve a more compact and wideband design that could be easily printed <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref20" id="context_ref_20_3b">[20]</a>â<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref21" id="context_ref_21_3b">[21]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref22" id="context_ref_22_3b">[22]</a>. A CPW-G on the top and bottom layers is extremely suitable at shielding the antenna and the sensor data bus from interfering noise that may have coupled into the shared power supply traces in the bottom layer and also due to the digital switching within the MCU on the top layer <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref23" id="context_ref_23_3b">[23]</a>. In addition, the CPW-G feed line could also allow a matching network to be implemented between the PA and antenna in the event of a possible mismatch between the two. The monopole-based sensor module topology is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig12" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 12</a>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig12"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808172/4808172-fig-12-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808172/4808172-fig-12-small.gif" alt="Figure 12" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 12. </b><fig><p>Monopole-based module topology.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4808172/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>The entire topology, shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig12" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 12</a>, was also simulated using Ansoft's High Frequency Structure Simulator (HFSS) 3-D electromagnetic (EM) tool. Multipoint grounds (RF and LF) were used for this design for better isolation between the digital switching occurring in the MCU and RF transmission <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref23" id="context_ref_23_3b">[23]</a>. RF chokes (L1 and L2) simulated as lumped RLC boundaries were once again used to isolate the two grounds, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig12" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 12</a>. A lumped port was used as the RF source to replicate the PA for the simulation. The antenna was matched to an impedance of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-20-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-224" role="math" style="width: 7.511em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 6.73em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1006.67em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-225"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-226" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">60.1</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-227" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">â</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-228" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic; padding-left: 0.243em;">j</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-229" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">73.51</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-230" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Â </span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-231" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Î©</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-20">60.1-j73.51\ \Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-21-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-232" role="math" style="width: 3.967em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.547em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1003.43em 2.706em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-233"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-234" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-235"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.766em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-236"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-237"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-238" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-239"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-240"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-241"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-242"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-243" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">L</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-244" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">â</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-245" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">o</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-246" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">p</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-247" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-248" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.397em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-21">({Z}_{{\rm L-opt}})</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, which is the reference at the PA output shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 8</a> at the design frequency of 904.4 MHz. The simulated return loss for the entire structure showed good wideband resonance of about 220 MHz around the design frequency of 904.4 MHz, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig13" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 13</a>. The maximum simulated directivity obtained was 2.6 dB. The measured and simulated radiation patterns are shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig14" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 14</a>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig13"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808172/4808172-fig-13-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808172/4808172-fig-13-small.gif" alt="Figure 13" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 13. </b><fig><p>Simulated return loss of the monopole antenna connected to the circuit.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4808172/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig14"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808172/4808172-fig-14-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808172/4808172-fig-14-small.gif" alt="Figure 14" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 14. </b><fig><p>Normalized 2-D far-field radiation plots of simulation and chamber measurement of the monopole-based printed sensor module.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4808172/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec4"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION IV.</div><h2>Fabrication and Assembly</h2></div><p>Once the system topology and antennas had been designed, the overall performance of the prototype board shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 7</a> was verified. The complete designs were then reproduced on paper using inket-printing technology. The antennas and the circuit layouts were printed and cured on paper using silver ink and the complete wireless sensor system comprising the IC (MCU+ transmitter), its discrete passive components, the temperature sensor, and an Li-ion cell for âstandaloneâ (autonomous) operation were assembled on it. The fabrication/assembly process is outlined in this section.</p><div class="section_2" id="sec4a"><h3>A. Inkjet-Printing Technique</h3><p>The proposed circuits for the wireless sensor module including the antennas and circuit layouts were designed and simulated using HFSS software, and fabricated using an inket-printing technique. In inkjet printing, the conductive silver ink droplets are directly sprayed from the inkjet nozzle onto the paper-based substrate, thus eliminating the waste generated using traditional photolithography techniques, which etch out unwanted metal at the end of the process <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_4a">[1]</a>.</p><p>A Dimatix DMP-2800 inkjet printer (printer) was used to carry out the inkjet printing. The conductor consisted of a conductive ink containing silver nanoparticles, which was sprayed onto a paper-based substrate using the inkjet printer to ensure good metal conductivity <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_4a">[1]</a>. To ensure maximum conductivity and antenna efficiency, the entire circuit was printed over with 12 layers of silver ink resulting in a conductor thickness of 12 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-22-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-249" role="math" style="width: 1.625em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.444em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.625em 1001.44em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-250"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-251" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Î¼</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-252"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-253"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-254"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-255"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-256" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">m</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-22">\mu{\hbox{m}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref14" id="context_ref_14_4a">[14]</a>.</p><p>The substrate was sintered continuously during the fabrication process at 60 Â°C using the hot base plate in the printing chamber of the printer shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig15" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 15</a>. The sintering process removed excess solvent and material impurities from the depositions and increased bonding between the silver ink and paper <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref24" id="context_ref_24_4a">[24]</a>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig15"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808172/4808172-fig-15-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808172/4808172-fig-15-small.gif" alt="Figure 15" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 15. </b><fig><p>Dimatix printing chamber.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4808172/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>The layers were printed using two different types of piezoelectric inket-printing cartridges. The high precision cartridge that sprayed 1-pL droplets was used to print finer areas in the circuit layout such as the IC traces and the PA interface to the antenna (150 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-23-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-257" role="math" style="width: 1.625em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.444em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.625em 1001.44em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-258"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-259" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Î¼</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-260"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-261"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-262"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-263"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-264" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">m</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-23">\mu{\hbox{m}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>). The 10-pL cartridge was used to print larger areas on the antenna and the RF ground planes/traces in both the monopole and dipole circuits to increase conductivity. This was done to minimize the gap between adjacently sprayed silver particles enabling a larger overlap during the annealing process and ensuring better conductivity of the printed structure. A close-up picture of the overlap between the printed ink layers using the 10-pL cartridge is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig16" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 16</a>. The printed structures were then cured in an industrial oven at 100 Â°C for 10 h. This was done with the intent to increase the conductivity of the printed structures toward the higher end of the conductivity range achievable with this process, which is between <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-24-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-265" role="math" style="width: 9.733em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 8.772em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.144em 1008.77em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-266"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-267"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-268"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-269"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-270"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-271" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">0.4</span></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-272" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">â¼</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-273" style="padding-left: 0.303em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-274"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-275"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-276"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-277" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">2.5</span></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-278" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">Ã</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-279" style="padding-left: 0.243em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.444em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.96em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-280"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-281"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-282"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-283"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-284" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">10</span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.441em; left: 1.024em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-285"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-286"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-287" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">7</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-288" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Â </span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-289"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-290"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-291"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-292"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-293" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">S/m</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.403em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-24">{\hbox{0.4}}\sim {\hbox{2.5}}\times {\hbox{10}}^{7}\ {\hbox{S/m}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_4a">[2]</a>. The entire printing process was repeated to print the individual layers used in the dipole-based (one layer) and monopole-based designs (two layers).
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig16"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808172/4808172-fig-16-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808172/4808172-fig-16-small.gif" alt="Figure 16" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 16. </b><fig><p>Fiducial camera image showing closeup of silver ink layers printed using 10-pL inkjet cartridge (zoom factor: Ã100).</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4808172/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec4b"><h3>B. Circuit Assembly</h3><p>Next, the wireless sensor modules were assembled on the printed circuit. The assembly process on silver pads proved to be the most challenging aspect in the design process. Given the low temperature tolerance of paper, the electronic components used, and the relative weaker adhesion of printed silver pads on paper, soldering had to be ruled out. Multiple assembly methods were experimented in order to find a reliable alternative for mounting components which include silver epoxies and conductive tapes.</p><p>The procedure for mounting components on the printed circuits was identical for both monopole- and dipole-based modules. The wireless sensor module using the monopole, due to its two-layer design, required additional steps to the assembly process. For the monopole-based module, the bottom layer containing the printed ground plane and the positive power supply trace was laminated to the top layer containing the printed circuit, monopole antenna, and signal feed line prior to the circuit assembly process. Roughly 5 lb/sq. in of pressure was applied on the two layers for 30 min until the bonding adhesive dried sufficiently.</p><p>Via-holes were then drilled through the laminated structure using a 400-<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-25-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-294" role="math" style="width: 1.625em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.444em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.625em 1001.44em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-295"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-296" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Î¼</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-297"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-298"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-299"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-300"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-301" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">m</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-25">\mu{\hbox{m}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> microdrill bit manufactured by LPKF A.G., Garbsen, Germany. Fiducial marks printed along the borders were used to ensure that the top and bottom layers of the monopole-based wireless sensor module were aligned properly. The drilled via-holes were then filled using silver epoxy. A small area of the adhesive was left to spill over from the via-holes across the top and bottom silver traces to ensure connection. The structure was then cured at 120 Â°C for 20 min.</p><p>Two different silver epoxies were investigated for making conductive electrical contacts between the circuit components and the printed silver traces given the unfeasibility of using solder on printed silver. The first type had a thinner texture prior to curing, which made it conducive to applying onto smaller circuit points. It could be easily applied to the finer interfaces between the components and printed silver traces. However, given its inability to hold components in place, nonconductive adhesive had to be applied first under the component terminals, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig17" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 17</a>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig17"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808172/4808172-fig-17-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808172/4808172-fig-17-small.gif" alt="Figure 17" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 17. </b><fig><p>Assembly process for components on printed silver pads using the Epo-Tek silver epoxy.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4808172/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig18"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808172/4808172-fig-18-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808172/4808172-fig-18-small.gif" alt="Figure 18" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 18. </b><fig><p>Silver epoxy textures before and after curing.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4808172/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>By comparison, the second type of epoxy used, which proved to be a better choice, had a denser texture providing a secure grip of the components prior to curing although it was harder to apply on finer areas in the circuit. A comparison between the two epoxy textures can be seen in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig18" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 18</a>. Both of the epoxies, after application, had to be cured in an oven to harden its textures and improve conductivity. The denser epoxy also has a much higher thermal conductivity of 12.7 W/mK compared to 2 W/mK for the thinner epoxy, resulting in a lower curing time, which was more conducive to the electrical components with lower temperature tolerances.</p><p>The entire assembly process had to be carried out in a multistep process <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_4b">[12]</a>. This was because the conductivity of the silver epoxy had a direct co-relation to its curing time and temperature, which contradicted with the limited temperature tolerance of the components used in the wireless transmitter. Due to this, the assembly of components was done in the order shown in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table2" class="fulltext-link">TableÂ II</a> <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_4b">[12]</a>. The curing time and temperature are also shown in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table2" class="fulltext-link">TableÂ II</a>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full table" id="table2"><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">TableÂ II </b>Curing Order, Temperature, and Time Used for Assembly Process<div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808172/4808172-table-2-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808172/4808172-table-2-small.gif" alt="Table " /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div></div>
<p></p></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec5"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION V.</div><h2>System-Level Performance</h2></div><p>Wireless link measurements were then performed with the assembled modules to verify their system-level performance. The wireless link measurements were carried out by placing the modules at different temperatures within an oven or refrigerator, and triggering them to transmit in the SENSE mode. On the receiver side, the ASK modulated wireless sensor information was captured using a wideband AN-400 RFID reader antenna connected to a Tektronix RSA 3408A real time spectrum analyzer (RTSA). The transmitter was kept at a distance greater than its far-field boundary from the receiver. The far-field boundary of the dipole and monopole-based modules were determined to be 3.8 and 5.4 cm using Fraunhofer's far-field equation shown in <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn2" href="#deqn2" class="fulltext-link">(2)</a> as follows <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref15" id="context_ref_15_5">[15]</a>: <disp-formula id="deqn2" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><div class="MathJax_Display"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-26-Frame" tabindex="0" style="width: 100%;"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-302" role="math" style="width: 100%; display: inline-block; min-width: 8.712em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 100%; height: 0px; font-size: 111%; min-width: 8.712em;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(2.465em 1004.45em 5.048em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em; width: 100%;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-303"><span class="mtable" id="MathJax-Span-304" style="min-width: 8.712em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 100%; height: 0px; min-width: 8.712em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: absolute; width: 4.568em; height: 0px; clip: rect(-1.559em 1004.45em 1.024em -999.997em); top: 0.003em; left: 50%; margin-left: -2.279em;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(2.465em 1004.45em 5.048em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.568em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(2.345em 1004.45em 4.928em -999.997em); top: -3.841em; left: 50%; margin-left: -2.279em;"><span class="mtd" id="MathJax-Span-314"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-315"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-316" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">R</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-317" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-318" style="padding-left: 0.303em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-319"><span class="mfrac" id="MathJax-Span-320"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.865em; height: 0px; margin-right: 0.123em; margin-left: 0.123em;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.006em 1001.75em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.682em; left: 50%; margin-left: -0.898em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-321"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-322" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-323"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.264em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-324" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">D</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.381em; left: 0.844em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-325"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-326"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-327" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.784em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.78em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-331"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-332" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">R</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-27">R</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the distance from the transmitter at which its far field region starts, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-28-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-333" role="math" style="width: 0.964em; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-28">D</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the largest dimension of the antenna, and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-29-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-336" role="math" style="width: 0.664em; top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-337"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-338" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Î»</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-29">\lambda</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the free-space wavelength at the transmit frequency of 904.4 MHz. The wireless sensor data captured by the RTSA were decoded and compared to the temperature obtained from a commercial noncontact infrared (IR) thermometer. The results have been summarized in this section.</p><div class="section_2" id="sec5a"><h3>A. Dipole-Based Wireless Sensor Module</h3><p>The assembled dipole-based wireless sensor module can be seen in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig19" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 19</a>. The transmitted signal measured by the RTSA from a distance of 4.26 m can be seen in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig20" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 20</a>, and was observed to be â48.07 dBm. The transmission obtained with the dipole-based sensor module presented in this paper was observed to be significantly better than the first prototype designed in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_5a">[12]</a> whose transmission from a distance of 0.3 m was only â69 dBm, shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig21" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 21</a>, and which was designed without accounting for the circuit and printing effects on the antenna.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig19"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808172/4808172-fig-19-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808172/4808172-fig-19-small.gif" alt="Figure 19" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 19. </b><fig><p>Dipole-based wireless sensor module on paper substrate using inket-printing technology.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4808172/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>

<p></p><p>Based on the transmission measurements carried out under laboratory conditions, a wireless link budget analysis was performed on the dipole-based sensor module from which its expected range was determined. The wireless link geometry used can be seen in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig22" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 22</a>. For the measurement setup used, the placement heights of the transmitter and receiver used were 1.17 (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-30-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-339" role="math" style="width: 1.024em; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-345"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-346"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-347" style="font-size: 70.7%; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-30">{h}_{t}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) and 0.97 (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-31-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-348" role="math" style="width: 1.084em;
