The transmitter was placed at a distance of 4.26 m (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-32-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-357" role="math" style="width: 0.604em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.544em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.54em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-358"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-359" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">d<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-32">d</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) from the receiver.

<p></p><p>For the measurement setup used, the maximum radius of the first Fresnel zone <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-33-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-360" role="math" style="width: 0.544em; The lengths <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-35-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-366" role="math" style="width: 0.964em; <p></p><p>The first Fresnel zone radius for the dipole-based module (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-38-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-435" role="math" style="width: 0.544em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.483em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.48em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-436"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-437" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">r</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.67em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-38">r</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) was determined to be approximately 0.5945 m, which is lower than the heights of the transmitter and receiver. Based on this assessment, the requirement of the clearance of the first Fresnel zone was satisfied and, due to which, the free-space loss model was the most suited for determining the wireless link budget for the dipole-based module <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref27" id="context_ref_27_5a">[27]</a>.</p><p>Using the free-space loss model for the measurement setup shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig22" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 22</a>, the maximum effective isotropic radiated power (EIRP) from a transmitter can be determined using <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn4" href="#deqn4" class="fulltext-link">(4)</a>. On the receive side, the AN-400 Reader antenna had a gain (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-39-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-438" role="math" style="width: 1.324em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.204em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.2em 2.526em -999.997em); padding-left: 0.243em;">20</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-499" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.183em;">log</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-500"></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-501" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-502" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Î»</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-503" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-504" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">.</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; For the measurement setup used thus far, the distance (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-42-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-505" role="math" style="width: 0.604em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.544em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.54em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-506"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-507" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">d<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-42">d</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) between the transmitter and receiver was low in proportion to their heights, thereby minimizing the effects of the ground. However, over longer ranges (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-43-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-508" role="math" style="width: 0.904em; Due to this, the two-ray beam tracing model was used to compute longer range distances of the transmitter since it better accounted for received signals that had bounced off the ground <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref26" id="context_ref_26_5a">[26]</a>. right: 0.003em;"><span class="mtd" id="mjx-eqn-${\hbox{(5)}}$"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-578"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-579"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-580"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-581"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-582"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-583"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-584"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-585" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(5)</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -1.397em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 3.403em;"></span></span></nobr></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-53">d=\left({{\hbox{EIRP}}\cdot G_{r}(h_{t}h_{r})^{2}\over P_{r}}\right)^{1\over 4}.\eqno{\hbox{(5)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">d=\left({{\hbox{EIRP}}\cdot G_{r}(h_{t}h_{r})^{2}\over P_{r}}\right)^{1\over 4}.\eqno{\hbox{(5)}}</span></span></disp-formula></p><p>In <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn5" href="#deqn5" class="fulltext-link">(5)</a>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-54-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-636" role="math" style="width: 1.144em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.02em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-637"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-638"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-639"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-640"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-641" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">P<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.123em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-642"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-643"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-644" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">r</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-54">{P}_{r}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the lowest power level detectable by a receiver, which is also known as the sensitivity of the receiver. A search for commercial transceivers that received ASK modulated signals at data rates of 5â10 kb/s, which are used for RFIDs and low power wireless sensing applications revealed sensitivities ranging from â65 to â111 dBm <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref29" id="context_ref_29_5a">[29]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref30" id="context_ref_30_5a">[30]</a>. Based on the receiver sensitivities found, for an omnidirectional antenna on the receiver side <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-55-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-645" role="math" style="width: 5.949em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 5.348em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1005.23em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-646"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-647" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-648"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.204em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-649"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-650"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-651" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">G</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.784em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-652"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-653"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-654" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">r</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-655" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-656" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">0</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-657" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Â </span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-658"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-659"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-660"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-661"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-662" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">dB</span></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-663" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-55">({G}_{r}=0\ {\hbox{dB}})</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, the dipole-based module would be expected to have a minimum range between 25.32 and 357.66 m using <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn5" href="#deqn5" class="fulltext-link">(5)</a>. In free space, this range would be between 15â2995 m for receivers with sensitivities ranging from â65 to â111 dBm, respectively.</p><p>In order to verify the correct operation of the dipole-based wireless sensor module, it was triggered to operate in the SENSING mode. The ASK modulated sensor information sent out by the module at different temperatures that was measured by the RTSA is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig24" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 24</a>. The transmitted sensor data shows good agreement with the measurements carried out with the digital IR thermometer. The digital IR thermometer has an accuracy of Â±2.5 Â°C. <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref31" id="context_ref_31_5a">[31]</a>.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec5b"><h3>B. Monopole-Based Wireless Sensor Module</h3><p>
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig24"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808172/4808172-fig-24-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808172/4808172-fig-24-small.gif" alt="Figure 24" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 24. </b><fig><p>ASK modulated temperature sensor data captured by the RTSA at room temperature (power versus time). Digital IR: temperature measured by the digital IR thermometer.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4808172/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig25"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808172/4808172-fig-25-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808172/4808172-fig-25-small.gif" alt="Figure 25" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 25. </b><fig><p>Monopole-based wireless sensor module (two layer).</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4808172/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div> The assembled monopole-based wireless sensor module can be seen in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig25" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 25</a>. The filled via-holes can be seen as smudges on the ground plane in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig25" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 25</a>. Wireless link measurements were carried out with the monopole-based wireless sensor module by placing them at different temperatures. The measurement setup was similar to the one used for the dipole-based modules. The transmitter and receive antenna were placed at heights of 0.86 (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-56-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-664" role="math" style="width: 1.024em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.9em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-665"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-666"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-667"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-668"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-669" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">h</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-670"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-671"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-672" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">t</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-56">{h}_{t}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) and 0.97 (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-57-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-673" role="math" style="width: 1.084em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.964em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.96em 2.526em -999.997em); clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-676"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-677"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-678" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">h</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-679"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-680"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-681" style="font-size: 70.7%; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.544em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.54em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-683"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-684" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">d<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-58">d</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) apart due to limitations with the measurement setup with the oven and refrigerator. The transmitted signal measured by the RTSA can be seen in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig26" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 26</a>, and was observed to be â26 dBm at a frequency of 904.4 MHz.
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig26"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808172/4808172-fig-26-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808172/4808172-fig-26-small.gif" alt="Figure 26" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 26. </b><fig><p>RTSA measured ASK modulated signal for the monopole-based module (power versus frequency).</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4808172/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>A wireless link budget similar to the one used for the dipole-based module was also carried out for the monopole-based module. The radius of the first Fresnel zone for the measurement setup used was determined to be 0.55 m, which was well cleared by the placement heights. Using the free-space loss model of <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn4" href="#deqn4" class="fulltext-link">(4)</a>, the EIRP transmitted from the monopole-based module was thereby determined to be 4.91 dBm.</p><p>The minimum range (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-59-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-685" role="math" style="width: 0.604em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.544em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.54em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-686"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-687" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">d<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-59">d</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) of the monopole-based wireless sensor modules using the two-ray beam tracing model were determined to be between 51.1â721.6 m using <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn5" href="#deqn5" class="fulltext-link">(5)</a> for receivers with sensitivities from â65 to â111 dBm, respectively, and an omnidirectional antenna <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-60-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-688" role="math" style="width: 5.949em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 5.348em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1005.23em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-689"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-690" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-691"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.204em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-692"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-693"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-694" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">G</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.784em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-695"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-696"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-697" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">r</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-698" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-699" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">0</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-700" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Â </span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-701"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-702"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-703"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-704"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-705" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">dB</span></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-706" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-60">({G}_{r}=0\ {\hbox{dB}})</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, respectively. However, in free space, the maximum range (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-61-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-707" role="math" style="width: 0.604em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.544em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.54em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-708"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-709" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">d<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-61">d</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) of the wireless sensor modules would increase to 82.66 on the lower end using <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn4" href="#deqn4" class="fulltext-link">(4)</a> for a receiver sensitivities of â65 dBm. However, for longer distances, the free-space model cannot be considered to be accurate since effects of the radius of the earth's curvature and environment need to be considered for distances over 10Â 000m <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref26" id="context_ref_26_5b">[26]</a>.</p><p>In order to verify the correct operation of the monopole-based wireless sensor module, it was placed at different temperatures while triggered to operate in the SENSING mode. The ASK modulated sensor information sent out by the module at different temperatures that was measured by the RTSA is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig27" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 27</a>. The transmitted sensor data shows good agreement with the measurements carried out with the digital IR thermometer. The digital IR thermometer has an accuracy of Â±2.5 Â°C <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref31" id="context_ref_31_5b">[31]</a>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig27"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808172/4808172-fig-27-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808172/4808172-fig-27-small.gif" alt="Figure 27" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 27. </b><fig><p>ASK modulated temperature sensor data captured by the RTSA from â2 Â°C to 42.4 Â°C (power versus time). Module: sensed temperature transmitted from module and captured by RTSA. Digital IR: temperature measured by the digital IR thermometer.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4808172/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>A comparison between the dipole- and monopole-based sensor modules can be seen in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table3" class="fulltext-link">TableÂ III</a>. Efforts to ensure an impedance match between the dipole and the RF PA with the circuit close to its feed, and reduce RF leakage from the RF to the non-RF digital side of the circuit did improve the performance of the dipole-based module. In addition, the use of a low-precision high-volume cartridge to increase conductivity of the antenna structure also helped in increasing the amount of power being transmitter by over 20 dB from its predecessor in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_5b">[12]</a>, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig21" class="fulltext-link">Figs.Â 21</a> and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig22" class="fulltext-link">22</a>. While the simulations revealed a directivity of 1.54 dB, a more thorough analysis needs to be performed to study the effects of the printing process and the module circuit on the gain of the dipole antenna since the EIRP of the sensor module was determined to be only â9.9 dBm.
</p><div class="figure figure-full table" id="table3"><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">TableÂ III </b>Performance Comparison Between the Dipole- and Monopole-Based Sensor Modules<div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808172/4808172-table-3-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4808172/4808172-table-3-small.gif" alt="Table " /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div></div>
<p></p><p>By comparison, the monopole through the use of its grounded structure offered a significantly convenient way of integrating the antenna with the module circuitry with a better match and isolation. The planar square shape of the monopole also increased the area of the overlap between adjacent printed layers that could potentially decrease losses in the radiating structure and increase the gain. This can be seen with the significantly higher EIRP (4.91 dBm) given out, and correspondingly, the longer range of the monopole-based sensor module.</p><p>In addition, the monopole-based structure also offered more wideband performance compared the dipole-based modules, as can be seen from their respective return losses in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig10" class="fulltext-link">Figs.Â 10</a> and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig13" class="fulltext-link">13</a>. The â10-dB return loss of the monopole covers all three frequency bands, 860, 904.4, and 925 MHz at which the RF PA in the transmitter could optimally operate. The dipole bandwidth was limited to only frequencies at 904.4 and 925 MHz.</p><p>While the size of the monopole and dipole radiating structure were comparable, the input feed of the monopole did significantly increase the overall size of the monopole-based sensor module. A shorter feed with a matching network could be used to decrease the dimension of the monopole-based module.</p><p>In addition, paper also offers excellent characteristics as a packaging material for sensors, especially temperature sensor considering its low thermal conductivity. The sensor measurements for both the dipole- and monopole-based sensor modules showed good agreement with digital IR thermometer that was used as a reference as was verified by its wireless link measurements.</p></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec6"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION VI.</div><h2>Conclusion</h2></div><p>Two different wireless sensor modules have been implemented on a paper substrate using inket-printing technology for the first time, and tested for wireless performance. The complete process including the system and antenna design, circuit layout, printing methodology, and assembly techniques that would potentially result in enhanced performance of the wireless sensor modules on paper was outlined. Wireless link measurements carried out on the complete prototypes on paper show acceptable performance on the communication and sensing side highlighting the feasibility of paper as a low-cost suitable eco-friendly packaging material as an active RFID-enabled wireless sensing platforms operating in the UHF range. Improved performance combined with the inherent cost and environmental advantages of paper over other substrates make paper-based wireless sensor modules an ideal choice for implementing large-scale RFID enables wireless sensor networks.</p></div>
<h3>ACKNOWLEDGMENT</h3><p>The authors would like to thank K. Rutkowski, SATIMO, Kennesaw, GA, for performing antenna radiation pattern measurements.</p></div></div>

<script>

function getCookie(name) {
	var nameEQ = name + "=";
	var ca = document.cookie.split(';');
	for(var i=0;i &lt; ca.length;i++) {
		var c = ca[i];
		while (c.charAt(0)==' ') c = c.substring(1,c.length);
		if (c.indexOf(nameEQ) == 0) return c.substring(nameEQ.length,c.length);
	}
	return null;
}

});
